# VRD annotation customisation instructions file

# Step 2 of the annotations customisation process: apply vr-specific
# changes, removals and appends.

# This instance of a VRD annotation customisation instructions file corresponds
# to Step 2 of the VRD annotation customisation process.  It allows analysts
# to precisely specify visual relationship (vr) changes and removals, as
# well as new vrs to be introduced (appended) to the existing annotations
# for an image.

# There is a protocol to which one must adhere when crafting a Step 2
# annotations customisation instructions file such as this. The basic
# protocol is described next.  For a given image:
#
# 1) Specify all your vr 'change' instructions, 'cvr...', first, if any; then
#    specify your 'remove' vr instructions, 'rvrxxx', if any; then, specify
#    your 'append' vr instructions, 'avrxxx', if any.  (The driver doesn't
#    enforce that 'appends' follow 'removes' because either order works, but
#    specifying 'removes' before 'appends' is a useful convention. The
#    essential thing is that all 'change' instructions are processed first.
#    This rule is enforced by the driver script.)
#
# 2) If you have multiple 'remove' vr, 'rvrxxx', instructions, for the same
#    image, specify them in DESCENDING order of index so that the execution
#    of one removal cannot invalidate the index of any subsequent vr yet
#    to be removed.

# There is a more subtle aspect to the protocol which one must be aware of
# and adhere to when specifying one's 'change' instructions for an image.
# If you specify multiple 'change' instructions for the same vr, you MUST
# repeat the same vr index value for that vr across your multiple
# 'change' instructions. Equally important, you MUST also reflect the
# sequence of changes you apply to a vr in the 'expected vr template', which
# has the form ('subject', 'predicate', 'object'), that is an essential part
# of every 'change', 'cvr...', instruction. If you fail to do this
# accurately, the driver script that processes this annotations
# customisation instructions file will detect a mismatch between the
# actual state of the vr targetted for change (as indicated by the value of
# the specified vr index in the 2nd component of the 'change' instruction)
# and the 'expected vr template' specified in the 3rd component of the 'change'
# instruction. Requiring users to specify both the index of the target vr
# they want to change AND their expectation as to the state of that vr
# is a SAFETY mechanism that has been built in to help prevent users from
# inadvertently specifying changes for the wrong visual relationship.
# Whenever the actual vr corresponding to the specified vr index value does
# NOT match the 'expected vr template' in the instruction, the driver script
# detects the mismatch and immediately aborts processing.

#
# object class: 'plate'
#

# 'plate' is used to refer to objects with very diverse
# meanings:
# 1 dishware plate
# 2 license plate (of a vehicle)
# 3 baseball plate (in a baseball diamond)
# 4 name plate or plaque
# 5 metal plate in ground
#
# We standardise the meaning of 'plate' to case (1): dishware plate
# We introduced object class 'license plate' for case (2)
# We introduced object class 'baseball plate' for case (3)
# We remove visual relationships for cases (4) and (5)

#
# object class: 'luggage'
#

# there is heavy overlap between 'luggage' and 'suitcase'; we
# decided to standardise the meaning of 'luggage' to refer to collections
# of multiple suitcases / duffle bags / etc..  Single suitcases
# labelled as 'luggage' are reclassified to 'suitcase'.

#
# -------------
# Customisations in relation to an analysis of the distinct predicates used
# with a specific pair of 'subject' and 'object' object classes.
# Example: ('wheel', X, 'motorcycle') yields X = {'under', 'beneath', 'on'}.
# Predicates 'under' and 'beneath' feel *wrong* because they ignore the
# *part of* nature of the relationship between a wheel and the motorcycle of
# which it is a part.
# -------------
#
